    <li> For the last three years I&#x27;ve been using the [[ASIN:B000W405SG Philips Norelco NT9110 Precision Nose and Ear Trimmer]]. I liked its versatility (the eyebrow comb in particular) and how it could reach in further than the rotary-style trimmer.  However, it started to jam on a regular basis and eventually broke, so I bought the Panasonic ER430K as a replacement.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First, that mirror cap.  It seems Panasonic read the complaints of other reviewers that there were no instructions to remove the protective film.  On mine, there was a big \\&quot;Peel off\\&quot; printed on this film.  That said, the reflective cap didn&#x27;t seem to be useful - I tried various angles and it didn&#x27;t add any value for me.  But that wasn&#x27;t why I bought it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The trimmer itself works well, though as I note above it doesn&#x27;t reach in quite as far as my old Norelco. I like that it is washable, though I&#x27;d think that using it in the shower would be self-defeating as the hairs would not stick out well, but perhaps I should try it some day.  It is easy to disassemble and wash out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The vacuum is a nice touch - I have a Philips beard trimmer with a vacuum - and I could see the hair clippings on the filter screen.  I never had an issue with nose hair clippings irritating my nose, but evidently some do and the ER430K seems to remove a good amount of the hair.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Panasonic&#x27;s instructions suggest that you can use this trimmer on eyebrows, mustaches, etc.  I suppose you can, yes, but with no ability to control cut length I&#x27;m not sure why you would.  That said, it works well at trimming stray hairs wherever they may be.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A nice touch is the zippered carrying bag.  It&#x27;s also nice to know that the removable parts can be ordered separately should they break, wear out or get lost.</li>
    <li> I just totally changed my review of this. Initially it seemed to cut well, and I posted a response based on that. Well, there was a slight change in my viewpoint and now I have sent it to the landfill. The first problem was that although it did initially cut well, I have no idea how but it also cut something in my nose. Thinking I had hit it at the perfect angle at the perfect time, I blew it off as nothing to worry about. Then it happened again and again. At that point I was very conscious of how I used it. That was the first downfall. The next was what someone else had stated--- Panasonic is all about the vacuum portion of it--- with that, it doesn&#x27;t do much for me and the other part of that is the cutters just simply didn&#x27;t last. I have been using it over 18-months and I noticed that it makes a lot of noise and just doesn&#x27;t cut correctly. With that, since my previous two were Wahl and they performed OK, I was on the lookout for something else that may work better. I even entertained the thought if a manual version, but I couldn&#x27;t honestly seeing it work they way I wanted it to, plus it would take two hands at once--- maybe I&#x27;ll try it someday, but not now.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So what I went and tried was an Andis 13430. It looks like in more than one way like a Wahl--- maybe it is, maybe not. Either way, for under $10 I have used it a couple of times and it works much better than the Panasonic. No propensity to nick or cut. Also the resonant frequency that it naturally vibrates at makes my nose tickle less... maybe it is the Panasonic vacuum thing, but either way I sent the Panasonic packing and moved on. I do not expect these things to work perfect, but they should work to some extent. I would have thought more from Panasonic, but for this it is worth looking at something else.</li>

It takes about ten minutes of use to get rid of all hairs. First you glide it on the interior surface of each nostril pushing it up and down and rotating it about ten degrees nine times. Then you use your index finger to press the tip of your nose towards your face. This changes the shape of your nostrils. You then angle the device about 20 degrees with respect to the vertical and do the above mentioned ritual. Then angel the trimmer 45 degrees to the vertical and to it all again.      Then you check the results. Insert your thumb in each nostril and put your index finger on the outside of the nose. Press them together and pull them towards the opening. This will reveal hairs that are still too long.     If you have not yet died of boredom, repeat all of the above ritual but just in the are of the newly discovered long hairs.</li>

    <li> I received the trimmer today.  It came in an easy cardboard container to open, and what you get is the trimmer, and a black felt bag for I guess if you travel, or if you choose to store it in the bag when at home.  You also need to have a AA battery to insert. In order to insert the battery, the instructions says to turn counterclockwise and match the line A with B, and pull to open.  Course, with me being literal, I tried to find the letter A and B to match it up but couldn&#x27;t.  There is no A or B.  A is a not so noticeable line on the bottom &amp;#34;firm&amp;#34; part of the trimmer.  It&#x27;s on the little &amp;#34;spoke&amp;#34; next to the screw (but you don&#x27;t unscrew it).  B is the battery cap that has the Model Number, and on the cap, is an arrow that points to a &amp;#34;dot&amp;#34;.  The &amp;#34;dot&amp;#34; is B, so you line up the DOT with the line on the spoke, and then you pull.  Doing a few times you don&#x27;t even need to look.  And it is hard to see so make sure you have some light and/reading glasses (if you need it) but again, once you do it one time, it&#x27;s so easy to remove and replace the battery.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also, reading the instructions, to perform maintenance on it, you need to remove 5 separate things (including the cover) sot hat you can clean the outer blade and inner blade, and filter.  The last item is the housing for the outer blade. Besides blowing to remove the hair, it says to use a soft tissue and gently wipe the blades and it says it can be washed in water.  Course I don&#x27;t know if its totally waterproof so I would take out the battery just in case if you were to go that route.  It also says if used once a week, for 1 min, the blade should last 3 years.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you&#x27;re like me, I was a little nervous about taking each item apart to clean as I think I might not be able to put them together again. I tried couple of times and again, after a while, it should be easy to maintain. The instructions are pretty clear on how the separate pieces.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So anyways, the first time I used it to remove the nose hair, I gotta say, it sure tickled.
